Last comment 2026-04-22 Re: [RFC PATCH v2 0/4] mm/zsmalloc: reduce zs_free() latency on swap release path Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch introduces a new function zs_free_deferred() for asynchronous handle freeing in zsmalloc. The original implementation of locking, grabbing a handle, and unlocking one at a time is inefficient and can be improved by using a workqueue or per-cpu-fying the batches/queues to reduce concurrency issues. An alternative approach suggested is to use two arrays of handles, swapping them under a lock when the defer worker is woken up, and then freeing the handles in the old array.

4 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants
Kairui Song ↳ replying to Nhat Pham Reviewed-by Needs Work LLM
Reviewer Kairui Song noted that zs_free() acquires pool->lock while compaction writes-acquires the same lock, causing contention between compaction and zs free-ers, and requested a perf trace on process teardown to determine if async zs-freeing is necessary or if zsmalloc's poor scalability in the free path can be addressed. Reviewer Kairui Song noted that freeing a swap entry also releases the backing compression data, which can lead to slower memory pressure reduction due to fragmentation and the need to free many swap entries for each folio. Reviewer Kairui Song suggested implementing a bulk zs_free() operation to reduce the number of individual frees and potentially improve performance. They also expressed concerns about the potential drawbacks of asynchronous freeing, including increased worker overhead and delayed memory pressure. Reviewer suggested optimizing zs_free() by using a percpu queue and attempting to free the whole queue under a read lock if successful
Show original comment 
Thanks for adding me to the Cc list :), Barry started this idea with
ZRAM, which looks very interesting to me.

---

It's not about decompression. I think what Wenchao means here is that:
freeing the swap entry also releases the backing compression data, but
compared to freeing an actual folio (which bring back a free folio to
reduce memory pressure), you may need to free a lot of swap entries to
free one whole folio, because the compressed data could be much
smaller than folio and with fragmentation. And swap entry freeing is
still not fast enough to be ignored.

---

That's a very nice insight. I had an idea previously that can we have
something like a zs free bulk? Freeing handles one by one does seem
expensive.
https://lore.kernel.org/linux-mm/adt3Q_SRToF6fb3W@KASONG-MC4/

It might be tricky to do so though.

It will be best if we can speed up everything, doing things async
doesn't reduce the total amount of work, and might cause more trouble
like worker overhead or delayed freeing causing more memory pressure,
if the workqueue didn't run in time. Or maybe a process is almost
completely swapped out, then this won't help at all.

I'm not against the async idea, they might combine well.

---

That's interesting, when I mentioned zs free bulk I was thinking that,
if we have a percpu queue, at least we may try read lock that on every
enqueue, free the whole queue if successful, then release the lock.
I'm sure there are more ways to optimize that, just a random idea :)

Completely agree! I was thinking about batching the free operations
for zsmalloc. Right now seems like even if we have a contiguous range
of swap slots to be freed, we call one
zram_slot_free_notify/zswap_invalidate at a time, which then call
zs_free one at a time? I wonder if there's any batching opportunity
here. Might be complicated with the pool lock and class lock dance in
zs_free() though :)

And yeah the async stuff is orthogonal too.

---

Yep! Would be nice to have some perf trace to pinpoint where the overhead is.

On my end, I perfed the free phase of usemem. It varies a bit based on
exact build config, kernel version, or even between runs, but the
cheapest I've seen for the pool lock contention overhead is about 3%
of the free phase (this is on baseline, not vswap kernel). That's
pretty big (bigger than vswap overhead even on the kernels with vswap,
which is kinda silly). Obviously the host was very overcommitted, so
compaction was running in the background at the same time, but
still...

Xueyuan Chen ↳ replying to Nhat Pham Inline Review Reviewed-by Needs Work LLM
Reviewer Xueyuan Chen noted that the current implementation of zsmalloc free operations may not be optimized for contiguous ranges of swap slots to be freed, suggesting batching opportunities to reduce overhead. The reviewer noted that free_zspage() acquires the class->lock while holding the zone->lock, creating a nested lock dependency and significantly extending the hold time of the class->lock, which causes other CPUs to wait longer.
Show original comment 
On Tue, Apr 21, 2026 at 11:25:17AM -0700, Nhat Pham wrote:

[...]

---

Hi Nhat,

Currently, free_zspage() is called while holding the class->lock. 
However, free_zspage() eventually invokes folio_put(), which may acquire
the zone->lock.

This creates a nested lock dependency. If multiple CPUs contend for the
same class->lock and the current holder is stalled waiting for the
zone->lock, it significantly extends the hold time of the class->lock.
This causes other CPUs to wait much longer.

Here is the ftrace data showing the severe contention on class->lock.
Under contention, the time spent in queued_spin_lock_slowpath() jumps 
from ~1.3us to over 30us, significantly increasing the total latency
of zs_free().

  7)               |  zs_free() {
  7)   0.220 us    |    _raw_read_lock();
  7)               |    _raw_spin_lock() {
  7)   1.320 us    |      queued_spin_lock_slowpath();
  7)   1.820 us    |    }
  7)   0.170 us    |    _raw_read_unlock();
  7)   0.170 us    |    obj_free();
  7)   0.190 us    |    fix_fullness_group();
  7)   0.150 us    |    _raw_spin_unlock();
  7)   0.170 us    |    kmem_cache_free();
  7)   4.610 us    |  }

---------------------------------------------------------

  7)               |  zs_free() {
  7)   0.230 us    |    _raw_read_lock();
  7)               |    _raw_spin_lock() {
  7) + 30.100 us   |      queued_spin_lock_slowpath();
  7) + 30.600 us   |    }
  7)   0.200 us    |    _raw_read_unlock();
  7)   0.170 us    |    obj_free();
  7)   0.170 us    |    fix_fullness_group();
  7)   0.170 us    |    _raw_spin_unlock();
  7)   0.210 us    |    kmem_cache_free();
  7) + 33.850 us   |  }

Best regards,
Xueyuan
View on lore ↗
Signals: requested changes, nested lock dependency, significantly extends the hold time
Last comment 2026-04-22 Re: [RFC PATCH v2 0/4] mm/zsmalloc: reduce zs_free() latency on swap release path Neutral LLM (per-reviewer)

This patch introduces a new function zs_free_deferred() for asynchronous handle freeing in zsmalloc. The original implementation of locking, grabbing a handle, and unlocking one at a time is inefficient and can be improved by using a workqueue or per-cpu-fying the batches/queues to reduce concurrency issues. An alternative approach suggested is to use two arrays of handles, swapping them under a lock when the defer worker is woken up, and then freeing the handles in the old array.

Last comment 2026-04-22 Re: [RFC PATCH v2 0/4] mm/zsmalloc: reduce zs_free() latency on swap release path Neutral LLM

This patch introduces a new function zs_free_deferred() for asynchronous handle freeing in zsmalloc. The original implementation of locking, grabbing a handle, and unlocking one at a time is inefficient and can be improved by using a workqueue or per-cpu-fying the batches/queues to reduce concurrency issues. An alternative approach suggested is to use two arrays of handles, swapping them under a lock when the defer worker is woken up, and then freeing the handles in the old array.

This patch addresses a potential deadlock in the rhashtable_free_and_destroy function by avoiding concurrent mutex lockers from the rht_deferred_worker function. Last comment 2026-04-24 Re: [PATCH] mm/lruvec: preemptively free dead folios during lru_add drain Neutral LLM

This patch optimizes the Linux kernel's memory management by preemptively freeing dead folios during the lru_add process, which reduces lock contention and improves system performance. The patch identifies that a significant portion of observable lruvec lock contention occurs when dead folios are present in lru_add batches at drain time, leading to unnecessary lock acquisitions. To address this issue, the patch uses folio_ref_freeze() to filter out dead folios before they enter the LRU and moves them onto a temporary batch for deferred cleanup. The patch was tested on a production workload and showed significant improvements in system-wide memory stats, including reduced direct reclaim scanning, allocation stalls, compaction stalls, and page frees.

2 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants

Reviewer Barry Song pointed out that the patch does not handle the case where a folio is being freed while it's still locked, which can lead to a deadlock situation.

Last comment 2026-04-23 Re: [PATCH] mm/vmscan: add balance_pgdat begin/end tracepoints Neutral LLM

Patch adds balance_pgdat begin/end tracepoints for mm/vmscan, with a discussion about tracing highest_zoneidx at the end.

2 reviewer comments — 0 participants
0 participants
Shakeel Butt Neutral LLM
Raised a question about whether highest_zoneidx needs to be traced at the end of balance_pgdat(), and suggested adding reasoning in the commit message.
Show original comment 
On Fri, Apr 24, 2026 at 08:46:24AM +0800, SUVONOV BUNYOD wrote:
> Thank you for reviewing Shakeel,
> 
> > Do we need to trace highest_zoneidx at the end? Can it change within
> > balance_pgdat()?
> 
> highest_zoneidx does not change within a balance_pgdat() invocation. It
> is passed in as an argument and remains the classzone bound used for the
> balancing checks throughout the function.
> 
> I kept highest_zoneidx in the end tracepoint to make the outcome event
> self-contained. In principle, begin/end correlation is possible, but
> under sustained memory pressure kswapd reclaim can be frequent enough
> that consumers may prefer to analyze end events directly, and any
> dependence on matching begin/end becomes less convenient and less robust
> in the presence of filtering or dropped trace records.
> 
> Since nr_reclaimed and the final order are only known at the end, having
> highest_zoneidx there allows end-only analysis without correlating with
> the begin event.
> 
> For example, it lets users answer questions like:
> - this pass reclaimed too much or too little memory; what highest_zoneidx
> did that result correspond to?
> - how much reclaim was done when balancing up to ZONE_NORMAL vs other
> classzone bounds?
> - when highest_zoneidx == ZONE_NORMAL, how often did reclaim finish at
> order=0?
> 
> So it is there because it provides context for the end-of-reclaim result.
> Do you think this is sufficient justification? If not, then I can drop it
> from the end tracepoint in v2.

I think it is ok but let's add this reasoning in the commit message.
Signals: QUESTION
Bunyod Suvonov ↳ replying to Shakeel Butt Positive LLM
Provided justification for tracing highest_zoneidx at the end, citing benefits for users who want to analyze end events directly and without correlating with begin events.
